        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer720099328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12056265984453966307"><i>Written April 17, 2014</i><br/><br/><b>4 1/2 Stars - Jeez, Ms. Phillips has the talent to write wonderful charming romances.</b><br/><br/>After reading two amazing books by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41313.Susan_Elizabeth_Phillips' title='Susan Elizabeth Phillips' rel='nofollow noopener'>Susan Elizabeth Phillips</a> was it time for the third. <i>It Had to Be You</i> recommended by my friend and fellow citizen <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260057416?book_show_action=false&page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Susanne (5 stars)</a>. The very best book by this author, according to her.<br/><br/><a href='http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <a href='http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <a href='http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <a href='http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b><i>It Had to Be You</i> is a 20 years old romance from 1994</b>. ~ Already with ratings from more than 27.800 readers on goodreads is this SEP's most popular book her</span>
  <span id="freeText12056265984453966307" style="display:none"><i>Written April 17, 2014</i><br><br><b>4 1/2 Stars - Jeez, Ms. Phillips has the talent to write wonderful charming romances.</b><br><br>After reading two amazing books by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41313.Susan_Elizabeth_Phillips" title="Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Susan Elizabeth Phillips</a> was it time for the third. <i>It Had to Be You</i> recommended by my friend and fellow citizen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260057416?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Susanne (5 stars)</a>. The very best book by this author, according to her.<br><br><a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="http://yoursmiles.org/t-heart.php?page=3" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397518236ra/9286620.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b><i>It Had to Be You</i> is a 20 years old romance from 1994</b>. ~ Already with ratings from more than 27.800 readers on goodreads is this SEP's most popular book here. ~ Further reviews and ratings, feels almost unnecessary. I'll try to keep myself short (..if that is possible?)<br><br>***********************************************<br><br><b>Phoebe Somerville, the outrageous, beautiful, blonde, <i>Marilyn Monroe</i>-like knockout</b>, inherits a professional football team from her recently deceased father. A complete surprise for her and for everyone else. She has not been her father's favorite daughter...ever. <br><br>After years of avoiding her old hometown and her father, Phoebe is now (as a 32 year old), forced to very reluctant return "home". She has to take care of a big football team, the staff, new dollar contracts, unsympathetic huge men and also a younger unfriendly teenage half-sister she barely knows. ~ And Phoebe knows exactly nothing about something so totally uninteresting as football. <br><blockquote>
<a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/albums/w615/Li64/Wear/shoes/?action=view&amp;current=388429ada5446c14023decc04f2fc535_zpsecc00914.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397525605i/9287634.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>‘She was without a doubt, the most worthless, spineless, silliest excuse for a human being he'd ever met in his life.’</blockquote><br><b>The <i>Chicago Stars</i>' head coach Dan Calebow</b>, is maybe not always a sexist jock taskmaster with a one-track mind, but he isn't that very glad in his teams new female <i>bimbo</i> owner. She is among the most stupid and ridiculous woman he ever met. Eye candy or not. Appearances may be deceiving. ~ He can not help but be, at least a bit, enchanted by this female beauty. <br><br><b>
  <u>The games start and the battle begins...</u>
</b> ~ Will Phoebe manages to persuade and make peace with this new strange sports-world? And Coach Dan, this temperamental man (a 37 years old former football player), is he able to manage his temper and lead the team to necessary new victories? And, perhaps most importantly, is Dan able to handle the new team-owner and perhaps even see something more in this flashy blonde? ~ The answer is: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Read and you will see.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>***********************************************<br><br><b>This started as a typical amusing <i>hate to love</i> romance</b>, in a good old-fashioned traditional <i>Austen</i> spirit. It starts with prejudices, preconceptions, an innate stubbornness and proudly characters, and of course several fun misunderstandings. But be just calm and patient, it turns right, and indeed then things hot up properly.<br><blockquote>
<a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/albums/w615/Li64/Cartoon/Couple%20drawings/?action=view&amp;current=9c3d5114213c63ed97ee9433f1473edb_zps20dfb7f1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397518236i/9286621.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>‘He seemed stunned, as if he'd never before been sassed by a woman. <i>God, he was cute. Cute and sexy and hunky and mean. Uhmm. Grrr.</i> ... It would take a lot of woman to tame a man like him.<br>She uncrossed her legs.<br>It would take a bed, too. (...)’</blockquote><br><b>Phoebe and Dan are really two opposites</b> and their thorny path towards a happy HEA is filled with funny jokes, hot moments (... everywhere), heartbreaking moments and an intriguing (football) plot with wonderful side characters. <br><blockquote>She: “I guess we're oil and water.” <br>He: “I'd say we're more like gasoline and a blowtorch.”</blockquote><br># <b>Dan is really all the tough men's Man with a capital letter</b>. A sweaty muscular and physically fit 37 year old in the gym can not be completely wrong. Or? ...I shouldn't say no. ~ He made me angry sometimes (so stupid unwise now and then), but finally was even I in his admirers league<br><br># <b>Phoebe is swank and sexy dressed, sparkly fun with pouty lips</b>, swinging blond hair and a woman's curves. Her hips get men on the case. A 'sassy' awesome lady... Moreover, she lurks them all for this girl has wits. ~ I liked her from the first page.<br><br>***********************************************<br><br><i>It Had To Be You</i> is perhaps written a quite long time ago, but it's just as fun to read today. A traditional contemporary romance - a stellar. A perfect feel good read. Hopefully you will chuckle, laugh, cry, and be amazed, surprised and just smile your silly "cozy smiling". And get the chance to live out all your emotions. I did at least. ~ It's heart, pain and a grand romantic final.<br><br><b>For god's sake, don't miss these lovely, sizzling hot</b>, super romantic books by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41313.Susan_Elizabeth_Phillips" title="Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Susan Elizabeth Phillips</a>. ~ This one was another recommended novel.<br><br><b>I LIKE - oh yes, yet another sparkling romantic diamond in this series</b><br><br><br>*****<br><i># BR with my (snowman) friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601922655?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen (4 1/2 stars)</a>, who listened to the audiobook. Thanks for joining me dear! ~ Our <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1766478-sep-buddyread-april-11-13-2104" rel="nofollow noopener">BR thread</a>.<br><br># I also need to highly recommend two other great (5 stars) romanses by this author: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719495741" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven, Texas (Chicago Stars, #2) </a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/610049373" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiss an Angel</a>.</i><br><br><i>At last...</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Animals/107f3ded-7112-4e24-9574-2a620052c110_zps8935d52f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397676490i/9310238.jpg" alt=" photo 107f3ded-7112-4e24-9574-2a620052c110_zps8935d52f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7463065-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145167p2/7463065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3636968255?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/7463065-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=toxicmasculinity-genderoles-andmore">toxicmasculinity-genderoles-andmore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=s-read-sport-romance">s-read-sport-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3636968255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18107755851807231906">It is a nice enough story, but it does feel <b>very dated</b> right now. This book was published in the 90's and it shows. The men are pretty sexist, including the male protagonist, which bothers me a lot. <br/>It is entertaining, although the start was a bit low for me, however, the way somethings were treated felt to me like things were not well rounded and opportunities were missed. <br/>Also, I don't know if it was because of the audiobook narrator, because it was another time (3 decades ago), or because it </span>
  <span id="freeText18107755851807231906" style="display:none">It is a nice enough story, but it does feel <b>very dated</b> right now. This book was published in the 90's and it shows. The men are pretty sexist, including the male protagonist, which bothers me a lot. <br />It is entertaining, although the start was a bit low for me, however, the way somethings were treated felt to me like things were not well rounded and opportunities were missed. <br />Also, I don't know if it was because of the audiobook narrator, because it was another time (3 decades ago), or because it was indeed written that way, but the male protagonist seemed older to me that what he was supposed to be, the way he expresses himself, the way he sees somethings, he just feels older to me, more like he was in his 40s rather than in his 30s. <br /><br /><b>The audiobook narrator</b> is very good, however her voice and tone in general aged the narration. A fresher tone and younger voice would have been more complementary to the story in my opinion.<br /><br /><b>The cover</b> is horrendous! Why would someone who is looking for a romance want to pick up a book with two boobs as the whole cover? I read this book because it was recommended to me, never in a million years would I have picked it up otherwise (not that romance books in general have appealing covers, but still). Whomever said it was a good idea lied, it is plain sabotage.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18107755851807231906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2065410187" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2065410187" />
    <a title="KatieV" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18620847-katiev"><img alt="KatieV" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390618322p2/18620847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065410187?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KatieV" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KatieV" href="/user/show/18620847-katiev">KatieV</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/9876503-it-had-to-be-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=genre-contemporary">genre-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=hero-extrmly-jealous">hero-extrmly-jealous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=hero-dominate-alpha">hero-dominate-alpha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=hero-protective">hero-protective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=pre-2k-oldie">pre-2k-oldie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=locale-america">locale-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=heroine-tortured-vulnerable">heroine-tortured-vulnerable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18620847-katiev?shelf=heroine-raped-by-other">heroine-raped-by-other</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065410187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10306067949682023621">I enjoyed it. Perhaps more so since I've been experiencing a dry spell of DNFs lately. <br/><br/>This book is contemporary-ish. It was published in '94 and definitely shows its age. I tend to enjoy the older books, but understand some want nothing to do with anything written last century. If you're one of those readers who is iffy about older romances, this probably isn't the book for you. Also there could potentially be triggers for sex abuse victims.<br/><br/>The beginning was odd. I can see any reader being turn</span>
  <span id="freeText10306067949682023621" style="display:none">I enjoyed it. Perhaps more so since I've been experiencing a dry spell of DNFs lately. <br /><br />This book is contemporary-ish. It was published in '94 and definitely shows its age. I tend to enjoy the older books, but understand some want nothing to do with anything written last century. If you're one of those readers who is iffy about older romances, this probably isn't the book for you. Also there could potentially be triggers for sex abuse victims.<br /><br />The beginning was odd. I can see any reader being turned off by the role play scene between the hero and his ex-wife. The way it was written made it seem that the hero was honestly interested in getting it on with a 16-year-old, rather than him playing along with one of his ex-wife's sexual power play scenarios. We also get to see the sex scene. I realize SEP was trying to provide context about the sexual relationship between the hero and his ex, as it did color things that happened between the H/h, but it could have been done in a different and less squicky way.<br /><br />The heroine was definitely over-the-top. I do wish her Betty Boop persona had been toned down some. I understood that she was using her sexuality as a power play, but some of her shenanigans were just silly and I felt attempting to play it for laughs took something away from what was a very tragic situation. As a rape victim, she felt powerless and developed a persona that used the sexual appeal she blamed for her rape as a shield. She even went through a brief period of promiscuity after the rape before taking refuge as the 'mistress' of a gay man and being celibate for 15 years. In most romance novels, a rape is almost always followed by sexual deep freeze. I admired SEP for bringing in the real fact that sometimes sex abuse victims become promiscuous. It seems counter-intuitive, but the human psyche is complex.<br /><br />The hero had his own issues based on an abusive childhood that encouraged anger as the only acceptable emotion. He had some epic explosions that made him look like a complete ass and he wasn't the most politically correct guy. He was obviously confused about women and what he needed/wanted. I couldn't help liking him though, he wasn't a bad guy and showed more compassion and understanding of the heroine's past than I expected based on some of his temper tantrums. He was a jealous guy, but he did not encompass the heroine's rapist or her post-rape behavior in his jealousy.<br /><br />This had it's faults, but it really drew me in. I was surprised since I care NOTHING about sports of any kind. It's fine that people enjoy watching, I just don't get it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10306067949682023621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16385598" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16385598" />
    <a title="Eastofoz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/939365-eastofoz"><img alt="Eastofoz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203907098p2/939365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16385598?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eastofoz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eastofoz" href="/user/show/939365-eastofoz">Eastofoz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Chick-lit with a side order of romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/939365-eastofoz?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16385598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7466635825884406823">I can’t say I really liked this book because it’s too chick-litty for me and I really dislike chick-lit so maybe for the chick-lit reader this is a good book. <br/><br/>I didn’t like the the hero or the heroine. The hero said too many mean and downright cruel things to the heroine that I don’t think could be taken back let alone forgiven. He also flew off the handle like some psycho for no reason. The heroine had too many issues and her whole switch in persona at the end was just too unbelievable. <br/><br/>There i</span>
  <span id="freeText7466635825884406823" style="display:none">I can’t say I really liked this book because it’s too chick-litty for me and I really dislike chick-lit so maybe for the chick-lit reader this is a good book. <br /><br />I didn’t like the the hero or the heroine. The hero said too many mean and downright cruel things to the heroine that I don’t think could be taken back let alone forgiven. He also flew off the handle like some psycho for no reason. The heroine had too many issues and her whole switch in persona at the end was just too unbelievable. <br /><br />There is way too much football filler in this novel too. I like a good sports romance but sometimes this went overboard. I guess you could say that it added to the story but it did nothing for the romance, apart from take time away from it (!) <br /><br />There is the odd bit of banter between Dan and Phoebe but there wasn’t enough to make me like their relationship. I enjoy a good love/hate romance, here however the heroine was emotionally hurt one time too many so I found it hard to believe that she could love Dan who should have been told to go and **bleep bleep** himself from the get-go :) <br /><br />The novel also has a very dated 90s feel to it –lots of references to AIDS, homophobia and having gay friends which just sounded too preachy to me. As for the other characters they were pretty good. The side story about the deranged father was very typical so that was a headache to read and I ended up skimming most of it.<br /><br />The last chapter was the nicest of the whole story and somewhat moving/funny but the epilogue was that gooey schmaltzy kind of drivel that I hate. <br /><br />Like I said, if you like chick-lit/romance then you may like this book. The writing is good overall (way too much narration in some parts though). It’s a toss-up between 2.5 - 3 stars for me. It’s just not my kind of read –-and a good thing to what with the number of books in this series (lol!)<br /></span>

<div id="review_2465488516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2465488516" />
    <a title="Amber’s reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36408777-amber-s-reading"><img alt="Amber’s reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507753197p2/36408777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2465488516?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=hate-to-love">hate-to-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=slow-burn">slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36408777-amber-s-reading?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2465488516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17695676213372147549">Re-read (actually listen). I love this book so much! Susan Elizabeth Phillips is comfort for my soul. I think I actually like the audiobook even more! The narrator Anna Fields is so wonderful to listen to. I can’t recommend SEP enough. If you have a good sense of humor, love romance and women’s fiction, you will love her books. <br/><br/><br/><br/>Original Review :<br/><br/>4.5 stars. Great sports romance that gave me everything I love about romance novels and nothing I dislike. <br/><br/>It was extremely well written and I flew throu</span>
  <span id="freeText17695676213372147549" style="display:none">Re-read (actually listen). I love this book so much! Susan Elizabeth Phillips is comfort for my soul. I think I actually like the audiobook even more! The narrator Anna Fields is so wonderful to listen to. I can’t recommend SEP enough. If you have a good sense of humor, love romance and women’s fiction, you will love her books. <br /><br /><br /><br />Original Review :<br /><br />4.5 stars. Great sports romance that gave me everything I love about romance novels and nothing I dislike. <br /><br />It was extremely well written and I flew through the pages. <br /><br />Maybe it’s because this book is 24 years old that I liked it so much. I read a lot of romance. At least a couple a week, and I feel that almost all of them have something that irks me. Whether it’s the character that’s scared of getting hurt and pushes the other character away to the way that the hero’s exes and all the women other than the heroine are portrayed as being sluts that throw themselves at the hero. This book didn’t have any of that. <br /><br />I also liked that this book was about the heroine being the underdog. I always love a good underdog story. Phoebe inherits her fathers NFL team with the stipulation that she has to win the playoffs to keep it. No one thinks she can succeed, even herself. And at first, she doesn’t really care enough to try. After enduring years of verbal abuse by her father and being raped, she makes a new life for herself and surrounds herself by men that can’t hurt her. She builds up walls and a whole different persona to deal with domineering men. But it’s all a facade to cope. <br /><br />Her strength is incredible and her ability to prove everyone wrong is inspiring. This is not a story of the hero saving the heroine. This is a story of a woman saving herself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17695676213372147549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1785343435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785343435" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1785343435?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785343435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9593532825710124841">A new-to-me author and a book written in 94. That's taking a chance. And I'm so glad I did. I thoroughly enjoyed it, though there are some elements that are going to divide based on audience experience and expectation, I think.<br/><br/>Phillips gives herself a hard hurdle from the start with Phoebe. She's a victim of rape who has since learned to manipulate sexual situations by turning all situations sexual with her in control. In other words, she maximizes her sexual broadcast to emphasize her desirabil</span>
  <span id="freeText9593532825710124841" style="display:none">A new-to-me author and a book written in 94. That's taking a chance. And I'm so glad I did. I thoroughly enjoyed it, though there are some elements that are going to divide based on audience experience and expectation, I think.<br /><br />Phillips gives herself a hard hurdle from the start with Phoebe. She's a victim of rape who has since learned to manipulate sexual situations by turning all situations sexual with her in control. In other words, she maximizes her sexual broadcast to emphasize her desirability in order to be able to turn <em>all men</em> down with the implication they don't meet her exacting standards. So she comes off as a tramp, deliberately, but does so to guard her celibacy. At the core, though, is a fear of men that has persisted for fifteen years. Part of the success of this strategy in her past is the discovery of high-profile gay men (artists, mainly) who use her as a beard—starting with one more than forty years her senior who ended up being more the father she never had than the lover they pretend he is. This being the mid 90s, AIDS plays a big role in her experience and so does sympathy for the gay community. This all works very well to set her up as an artsy socialite and the exact opposite of what the NFL world she finds herself in would value.<br /><br />Not content with the hangups in the heroine, Phillips doubles down with Dan; he's a nice guy in a manly profession whose ex-wife still wants him to play dominance games with her. He doesn't like the games, but the sex is good and he really doesn't want to return to the sexual smorgasbord of his youth as a famous football player. Which leaves him highly vulnerable to misunderstanding Phoebe's whipsaw sexuality and susceptible to traumatizing her further when he gets her mixed signals. Which is a really tricky line to walk and where personal background and experience will lead people with otherwise similar tastes to have vastly different perceptions of this book, I think. Personally, I found Dan's charm and kindness and care nine kind of engaging and I fell for him early and hard. Almost as hard as I fell for Phoebe. I've always been a sucker for the strong alpha with a kind heart and ready sympathy and Dan is all that and more. His concern while trying to decrypt Phoebe's signals had me from their first interactions and kept me through his inevitable missteps and apologies. That said, I would completely understand if others had a hard time with Dan's misreads and wrote him off as a result.<br /><br />There are one and a half drawbacks I had with the book, but they're relatively minor. The main drawback is the psycho weirdo stalking Dan and the couple of page-long sections from his viewpoint. I found those completely unnecessary and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the whole kidnapping to force a loss thing was just stupid. Phillips had already done a great job making that game meaningful and it could have easily been expressed better as a game with a lot on the line without adding stupid drama. That this is the only time I thought Phillips broke with reality in how professional football and the NFL would react doesn't help (cheating is a big fat hairy deal and there's no way Dan would have escaped hearings and been at least suspended during their course) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The half problem was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[making cousin Reed a moustache-twirling villain. There's a section a little bit in where we're given hope he isn't a complete waste, but that's quickly countered and I was sad to see Phillips go to stereotype there <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />As strongly engaged as I was (and able to pull me away from my New Orleans vacation to read), this was an easy five stars. The small detractions didn't pull it down enough to lower the rating.<br /><br /><strong>A note about Steamy</strong>: Three plus one explicit sex scenes put this on the high side of my tolerance, though only barely. That's mainly because they're so tightly tied to Phoebe's emotional recovery and they're exactly where Dan shines best. The plus one is a scene that lets the reader know the kind of games Dan has become used to with his ex. Which makes it a judgement call to include, but I think Phillips used it well so it doesn't trip my "sex with other people" pet peeve I usually have in romances.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9593532825710124841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I cried and I laughed and the ending was so sweet, so right. This book was not what I expected but so much better. My heart broke for Phoebe in the beginning of the book and to follow her growth and healing process was amazing.   <span id="freeText2532915131530119111" style="display:none">It was brilliant. I'm speechless and will not even try to write a review. It was terrible, and definitely not a feel good-cookie but so great. I cried and I laughed and the ending was so sweet, so right. This book was not what I expected but so much better. My heart broke for Phoebe in the beginning of the book and to follow her growth and healing process was amazing. It was so believable, so touching. <br /><br /><b>Updated 14/4/13</b><br /><br />It was just as great the second time around. Even though I remembered almost everything I could not put it down. IMHO it's Suzan Elizabeth Phillips very best book.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zc2LMAE5zXzcyMEjDnb7QwzGybPFYqevMMFap1X8mpbwuLE0+eo1hkjpEObb3iPscJ6QfDtYKm6QXIulSmwikg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1LbgJkedxxcL8Zp73C9h+aw8I6eO8gcaONEPMZS//Mrpw9oiv04/7Z/QS74Jh7lW0GR6aHDIituYTN4ziy9Ezg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer106599320969947681">SUSAN ELIZABETH PHILLIPS<br/><br/>Susan Elizabeth Phillips is the creator of the sports romance, beginning with her 1989 bestseller, FANCY PANTS. An internationally acclaimed author, her books have been published in over 30 languages. She’s the only four-time recipient of the Romance Writers of America’s prestigious Favorite Book of the Year Award, and a recipient of their Lifetime Achievement Award. <br/><br/>Susan'</span>
  <span id="freeText106599320969947681" style="display:none">SUSAN ELIZABETH PHILLIPS<br /><br />Susan Elizabeth Phillips is the creator of the sports romance, beginning with her 1989 bestseller, FANCY PANTS. An internationally acclaimed author, her books have been published in over 30 languages. She’s the only four-time recipient of the Romance Writers of America’s prestigious Favorite Book of the Year Award, and a recipient of their Lifetime Achievement Award. <br /><br />Susan's newest book, DANCE AWAY WITH ME, was published in hardcover, ebook and audiobook in June 2020. She is also the highly acclaimed author of both the CHICAGO STARS football series and the Wynette, Texas books. <br /><br />In addition to being a New York Times, Publisher’s Weekly, and USA Today bestseller, she is a hiker, lazy gardener, horrible singer, passable cook, passionate reader, wife, mother of two grown sons, and grandmother. <br /><br />You can visit Susan on Facebook, Twitter, Instagram or on her website.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/SusanElizabethPhillipsNovels">https://www.facebook.com/SusanElizabe...</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/sepauthor">https://twitter.com/sepauthor</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/SEPauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/SEPauthor/</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://susanelizabethphillips.com/">http://susanelizabethphillips.com/</a><br /><br /></span>
